Centauri A</i></td>\n<td>101.25</td>\n<td>4.36</td>\n<td>1.52\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>&#945; Centauri B</i></td>\n<td>147.58</td>\n<td>4.36</td>\n<td>0.50\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Procyon A</i></td>\n<td>154.06</td>\n<td>11.44</td>\n<td>6.94\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Vega</i></td>\n<td>167.39</td>\n<td>25.02</td>\n<td>50.05\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i> Altair</i></td>\n<td>176.67</td>\n<td>16.69</td>\n<td>10.70\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Fomalhaut A</i></td>\n<td>221.33</td>\n<td>25.13</td>\n<td>16.67\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Denebola</i></td>\n<td>325.56</td>\n<td>35.78</td>\n<td>14.66\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Castor A</i></td>\n<td>341.35</td>\n<td>50.98</td>\n<td>49.85\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>Epsilon Eridiani</i></td>\n<td>363.35</td>\n<td>10.50</td>\n<td>0.50\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li>Successive assists at &#945; Cen A and B could allow travel times to 75 yr to both stars.</li>\n<li>Lightsail has a nominal mass-to-surface ratio (&#963;<sub>nom</sub>) of 8.6&#215;10<sup>&#8722;4</sup> gram m<sup>&#8722;2</sup> for a nominal graphene-class sail.</li>\n<li>Area of the Lightsail, about 10<sup>5</sup> m<sup>2</sup> = (316 m)<sup>2</sup></li>\n<li>Velocity up to 37,300&#160;km s<sup>&#8722;1</sup> (12.5% c)</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-accelerated_fuel">Pre-accelerated fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Pre-accelerated fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Achieving start-stop interstellar trip times of less than a human lifetime require mass-ratios of between 1,000 and 1,000,000, even for the nearer stars. This could be achieved by multi-staged vehicles on a vast scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L.D._Jaffe_1963,_pp._49-58_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-L.D._Jaffe_1963,_pp._49-58-45">[45]</a></sup> Alternatively large linear accelerators could propel fuel to fission propelled space-vehicles, avoiding the limitations of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rocket_equation" title="Rocket equation">Rocket equation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interstellar_rendezvous_missions_employing_fission_propulsion_systems_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Interstellar_rendezvous_missions_employing_fission_propulsion_systems-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theoretical_concepts">Theoretical concepts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Theoretical concepts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Faster-than-light_travel">Faster-than-light travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Faster-than-light travel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg/220px-Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg/330px-Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg/440px-Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wormhole_travel_as_envisioned_by_Les_Bossinas_for_NASA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artist\'s depiction of a hypothetical <i>Wormhole Induction Propelled Spacecraft</i>, based loosely on the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Alcubierre_drive" title="Alcubierre drive">"warp drive"</a> paper of <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Alcubierre" title="Miguel Alcubierre">Miguel Alcubierre</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light" title="Faster-than-light">Faster-than-light</a></div>\n<p>Scientists and authors have postulated a number of ways by which it might be possible to surpass the speed of light, but even the most serious-minded of these are highly speculative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crawftl_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-crawftl-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is also debatable whether faster-than-light travel is physically possible, in part because of <a href="/wiki/Tachyonic_antitelephone" title="Tachyonic antitelephone">causality</a> concerns: travel faster than light may, under certain conditions, permit travel backwards in time within the context of <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Proposed mechanisms for <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light" title="Faster-than-light">faster-than-light</a> travel within the theory of general relativity require the existence of <a href="/wiki/Exotic_matter" title="Exotic matter">exotic matter</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crawftl_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-crawftl-59">[59]</a></sup> and it is not known if this could be produced in sufficient quantity.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Alcubierre_drive">Alcubierre drive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Alcubierre drive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alcubierre_drive" title="Alcubierre drive">Alcubierre drive</a></div>\n<p>In physics, the <a href="/wiki/Alcubierre_drive" title="Alcubierre drive">Alcubierre drive</a> is based on an argument, within the framework of <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> and without the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Wormhole" title="Wormhole">wormholes</a>, that it is possible to modify a spacetime in a way that allows a spaceship to travel with an arbitrarily large speed by a local expansion of spacetime behind the spaceship and an opposite contraction in front of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warp_Alcubierre_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Warp_Alcubierre-61">[61]</a></sup> Nevertheless, this concept would require the spaceship to incorporate a region of <a href="/wiki/Exotic_matter" title="Exotic matter">exotic matter</a>, or hypothetical concept of <a href="/wiki/Negative_mass" title="Negative mass">negative mass</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warp_Alcubierre_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Warp_Alcubierre-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Artificial_black_hole">Artificial black hole</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Artificial black hole">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_starship" title="Black hole starship">Black hole starship</a></div>\n<p>A theoretical idea for enabling interstellar travel is by propelling a starship by creating an artificial black hole and using a parabolic reflector to reflect its Hawking radiation. Although beyond current technological capabilities, a black hole starship offers some advantages compared to other possible methods. Getting the black hole to act as a power source and engine also requires a way to convert the Hawking radiation into energy and thrust. One potential method involves placing the hole at the focal point of a parabolic reflector attached to the ship, creating forward thrust. A slightly easier, but less efficient method would involve simply absorbing all the gamma radiation heading towards the fore of the ship to push it onwards, and let the rest shoot out the back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cranewestmoreland2009_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-cranewestmoreland2009-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Wormholes">Wormholes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Wormholes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Wormhole" title="Wormhole">Wormholes</a> are conjectural distortions in spacetime that theorists postulate could connect two arbitrary points in the universe, across an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Rosen_Bridge" title="Einstein&#8211;Rosen Bridge">Einstein&#8211;Rosen Bridge</a>. It is not known whether wormholes are possible in practice. Although there are solutions to the Einstein equation of general relativity that allow for wormholes, all of the currently known solutions involve some assumption, for example the existence of <a href="/wiki/Negative_mass" title="Negative mass">negative mass</a>, which may be unphysical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> However, Cramer <i>et al.</i> argue that such wormholes might have been created in the early universe, stabilized by <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_string" title="Cosmic string">cosmic string</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The general theory of wormholes is discussed by Visser in the book <i>Lorentzian Wormholes</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Designs_and_studies">Designs and studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Designs and studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enzmann_starship">Enzmann starship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Enzmann starship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Enzmann_starship" title="Enzmann starship">Enzmann starship</a></div>\n<p>The Enzmann starship, as detailed by <a href="/wiki/G._Harry_Stine" title="G. Harry Stine">G. Harry Stine</a> in the October 1973 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Analog_Science_Fiction_and_Fact" title="Analog Science Fiction and Fact">Analog</a></i>, was a design for a future <a href="/wiki/Starship" title="Starship">starship</a>, based on the ideas of Robert Duncan-Enzmann. The spacecraft itself as proposed used a 12,000,000 ton ball of frozen <a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium">deuterium</a> to power 12&#8211;24 thermonuclear pulse propulsion units. Twice as long as the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a> and assembled in-orbit, the spacecraft was part of a larger project preceded by <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_probe" title="Interstellar probe">interstellar probes</a> and telescopic observation of target star systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Project_Hyperion">Project Hyperion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Project Hyperion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Project Hyperion, one of the projects of <a href="/wiki/Icarus_Interstellar" title="Icarus Interstellar">Icarus Interstellar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_research">NASA research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: NASA research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration">NASA</a> has been researching interstellar travel since its formation, translating important foreign language papers and conducting early studies on applying fusion propulsion, in the 1960s, and laser propulsion, in the 1970s, to interstellar travel.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration">NASA</a> <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Propulsion_Physics_Program" title="Breakthrough Propulsion Physics Program">Breakthrough Propulsion Physics Program</a> (terminated in FY 2003 after a 6-year, $1.2-million study, because "No breakthroughs appear imminent.")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> identified some breakthroughs that are needed for interstellar travel to be possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAWarpDriveBreakthruTechs_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAWarpDriveBreakthruTechs-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_A._Landis" title="Geoffrey A. Landis">Geoffrey A. Landis</a> of NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Research_Center" title="Glenn Research Center">Glenn Research Center</a> states that a laser-powered interstellar sail ship could possibly be launched within 50 years, using new methods of space travel. "I&#160;think that ultimately we\'re going to do it, it\'s just a question of when and who," Landis said in an interview. Rockets are too slow to send humans on interstellar missions. Instead, he envisions interstellar craft with extensive sails, propelled by laser light to about one-tenth the speed of light. It would take such a ship about 43 years to reach Alpha Centauri if it passed through the system without stopping. Slowing down to stop at Alpha Centauri could increase the trip to 100 years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malik20020319_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malik20020319-72">[72]</a></sup> whereas a journey without slowing down raises the issue of making sufficiently accurate and useful observations and measurements during a fly-by.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="100_Year_Starship_study">100 Year Starship study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: 100 Year Starship study">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/100_Year_Starship" title="100 Year Starship">100 Year Starship</a> (100YSS) is the name of the overall effort that will, over the next century, work toward achieving interstellar travel. The effort will also go by the moniker 100YSS. The 100 Year Starship study is the name of a one-year project to assess the attributes of and lay the groundwork for an organization that can carry forward the 100 Year Starship vision.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harold_Sonny_White_(NASA_Scientist)" title="Harold Sonny White (NASA Scientist)">Harold ("Sonny") White</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> from NASA\'s Johnson Space Center is a member of <a href="/wiki/Icarus_Interstellar" title="Icarus Interstellar">Icarus Interstellar</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icarusinterstellar.org_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-icarusinterstellar.org-74">[74]</a></sup> the nonprofit foundation whose mission is to realize interstellar flight before the year 2100. At the 2012 meeting of 100YSS, he reported using a <a href="/wiki/White%E2%80%93Juday_warp-field_interferometer" title="White&#8211;Juday warp-field interferometer">laser to try to warp spacetime</a> by 1 part in 10 million with the aim of helping to make interstellar travel possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_designs">Other designs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Other designs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Project_Orion_(nuclear_propulsion)" title="Project Orion (nuclear propulsion)">Project Orion</a>, manned interstellar ship (1958&#8211;1968).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Project_Daedalus" title="Project Daedalus">Project Daedalus</a>, unmanned interstellar probe (1973&#8211;1978).</li>\n<li>Starwisp, unmanned interstellar probe (1985).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Project_Longshot" title="Project Longshot">Project Longshot</a>, unmanned interstellar probe (1987&#8211;1988).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Starseed_launcher" title="Starseed launcher">Starseed/launcher</a>, fleet of unmanned interstellar probes (1996)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Project_Valkyrie" title="Project Valkyrie">Project Valkyrie</a>, manned interstellar ship (2009)</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Icarus_(Interstellar_Probe_Design_Study)" title="Project Icarus (Interstellar Probe Design Study)">Project Icarus</a>, unmanned interstellar probe (2009&#8211;2014).</li>\n<li>Sun-diver, unmanned interstellar probe<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Starshot" title="Breakthrough Starshot">Breakthrough Starshot</a>, fleet of unmanned interstellar probes, announced in April 12, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Starshot_home_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Starshot_home-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concept\'_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-concept\'-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-profit_organizations">Non-profit organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Non-profit organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A few organisations dedicated to interstellar propulsion research and advocacy for the case exist worldwide. These are still  in their infancy, but are already backed up by a membership of a wide variety of scientists, students and professionals.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/100_Year_Starship" title="100 Year Starship">100 Year Starship</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Icarus_Interstellar" title="Icarus Interstellar">Icarus Interstellar</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icarusinterstellar.org_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-icarusinterstellar.org-74">[74]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tau_Zero_Foundation_(USA)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tau Zero Foundation (USA) (page does not exist)">Tau Zero Foundation (USA)</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-https://tauzero.aero_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-https://tauzero.aero-82">[82]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Initiative_for_Interstellar_Studies" title="Initiative for Interstellar Studies">Initiative for Interstellar Studies</a> (UK) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Fourth Millennium Foundation (Belgium) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Space Development Cooperative (Canada) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feasibility">Feasibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Feasibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The energy requirements make interstellar travel very difficult. It has been reported that at the 2008 Joint Propulsion Conference, multiple experts opined that it was improbable that humans would ever explore beyond the Solar System.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O&#8217;Neill_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-O&#8217;Neill-86">[86]</a></sup> Brice N. Cassenti, an associate professor with the Department of Engineering and Science at Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute, stated that at least 100 times the total energy output of the entire world [in a given year] would be required to send a probe to the nearest star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O&#8217;Neill_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-O&#8217;Neill-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Astrophysicist Sten Odenwald stated that the basic problem is that through intensive studies of thousands of detected exoplanets, most of the closest destinations within 50 light years do not yield Earth-like planets in the star\'s habitable zones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Odenwald_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Odenwald-87">[87]</a></sup> Given the multitrillion-dollar expense of some of the proposed technologies, travelers will have to spend up to 200 years traveling at 20% the speed of light to reach the best known destinations. Moreover, once the travelers arrive at their destination (by any means), they will not be able to travel down to the surface of the target world and set up a colony unless the atmosphere is non-lethal. The prospect of making such a journey, only to spend the rest of the colony\'s life inside a sealed habitat and venturing outside in a spacesuit, may eliminate many prospective targets from the list.\n</p><p>Moving at a speed close to the speed of light and encountering even a tiny stationary object like a grain of sand will have fatal consequences. For example, a gram of matter moving at 90% of the speed of light contains a kinetic energy corresponding to a small nuclear bomb (around 30kt TNT).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interstellar_missions_not_for_human_benefit">Interstellar missions not for human benefit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Interstellar missions not for human benefit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Explorative high-speed missions to <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Centauri" title="Alpha Centauri">Alpha Centauri</a>, as planned for by the <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Starshot" title="Breakthrough Starshot">Breakthrough Starshot initiative</a>, are projected to be realizable within the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> It is alternatively possible to plan for unmanned slow-cruising missions taking millennia to arrive. These probes would not be for human benefit in the sense that one can not foresee whether there would be anybody around on earth interested in then back-transmitted science data. An example would be the Genesis mission,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> which aims to bring unicellular life, in the spirit of <a href="/wiki/Directed_panspermia" title="Directed panspermia">directed panspermia</a>, to habitable but otherwise barren planets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Comparatively slow cruising Genesis probes, with a typical speed of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c/300}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mn>300</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c/300}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle c/300}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6b07c42a9bf1acfbee6ce2368cd911a9d460c78c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.657ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, corresponding to about <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 1000\\,{\\mbox{km/s}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>1000</mn>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mtext>km/s</mtext>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 1000\\,{\\mbox{km/s}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle 1000\\,{\\mbox{km/s}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d9f4c2ab9fcf590f71a8ff86c0b4e24472ba4f8" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.279ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, can be decelerated using a <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_sail" title="Magnetic sail">magnetic sail</a>. Unmanned missions not for human benefit would hence be feasible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_of_Earth-Like_planets">Discovery of Earth-Like planets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Discovery of Earth-Like planets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In February 2017, NASA announced that its <a href="/wiki/Spitzer_Space_Telescope" title="Spitzer Space Telescope">Spitzer Space Telescope</a> had revealed seven Earth-size planets in the TRAPPIST-1 system orbiting an ultra-cool dwarf star 40 light-years away from our solar system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_Press_Release_Feb_22nd_2017_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_Press_Release_Feb_22nd_2017-92">[92]</a></sup> Three of these planets are firmly located in the habitable zone, the area around the parent star where a rocky planet is most likely to have liquid water. The discovery sets a new record for greatest number of habitable-zone planets found around a single star outside our solar system. All of these seven planets could have liquid water &#8211; the key to life as we know it &#8211; under the right atmospheric conditions, but the chances are highest with the three in the habitable zone.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interstellar_travel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
